###begin p 62
###xml 7 11 7 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">leuW</italic>
###xml 171 179 171 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 234 238 234 238 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu3</sup>
###xml 277 285 277 285 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 343 347 343 347 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu3</sup>
###xml 384 389 384 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 485 491 485 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 496 508 496 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1 rnpA49</italic>
###xml 612 620 612 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
As the leuW-coding sequence is unique to this operon and differs significantly from the other seven leucine tRNAs, we initially probed the northern blot with the probe c (Figure 6A). As expected a band corresponding to the mature tRNALeu3 (M1) was observed in all the strains (Figure 6B, lanes 1-5). While both the RQ and PF of the mature tRNALeu3 were reduced only marginally in the rne-1 mutant compared to the wild-type control, the decreases were much more significant in both the rnpA49 and rne-1 rnpA49 mutants. Besides the mature tRNA band (M1), five other processing intermediates (I, II, IV, V and VII, Figure 6B, lanes 2-4) were observed in various genetic backgrounds.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 123 131 123 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 195 198 195 198 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 200 204 200 204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 209 213 209 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metU</italic>
###xml 323 331 323 331 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 385 389 385 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">leuW</italic>
###xml 458 466 458 466 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 603 609 591 597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 705 709 693 697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
In order to determine the composition of these intermediates, we hybridized the blot with two additional oligonucleotides (Figure 6A-a and b) that were complementary to the 5' non-coding and tRNAMet (metT and metU)-coding regions, respectively. Both of these probes hybridized to bands I, II, IV and V but not to band VII (Figure 6B, lanes 8-9 and 13-14), which was thus identified as leuW with an unprocessed 5' end that occurred in the absence of RNase P (Figure 6B, lane 3). However, both the probes a and b hybridized to a new processing intermediate (VI) of approximately125 nt that was present in rnpA49 mutants (lanes 8-9 and 13-14) and was absent in the c-probed blot. Thus species VI represented metT containing an unprocessed 5' end.
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 108 113 108 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 184 187 184 187 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 220 228 220 228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 283 287 283 287 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu3</sup>
###xml 388 391 388 391 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 499 502 499 502 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 504 512 504 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
Furthermore, probe b hybridized to an additional high-molecular weight processing intermediate (III) in the rne-1 mutant (lane 12), and, as expected, also hybridized to the mature tRNAMet in all genetic backgrounds (M2, Figure 6B, lanes 11-15). Similar to what was observed with tRNALeu3 (M1), inactivation of RNase E led to only a small reduction in the relative level of the mature tRNAMet (lane 12). In contrast, the loss of RNase P activity had a much greater effect on the amount of mature tRNAMet (Figure 6B, lanes 13 and 14).
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 41 49 41 49 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 148 156 148 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 251 257 251 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 273 281 273 281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 437 449 437 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1 rnpA49</italic>
###xml 465 473 465 473 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 622 631 622 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 644 651 644 651 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 781 785 781 785 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 882 885 870 873 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 894 898 882 886 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu3</sup>
###xml 905 908 893 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne</italic>
###xml 963 968 951 956 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 977 985 965 973 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
Probing the blot with oligonucleotide i (Figure 6A), which was complementary to the terminator sequences of the operon, identified bands I and III (Figure 6B) in all strains defective in RNase E (data not shown). Since these bands were missing in the rnpA49 single mutant (Figure 6B, data not shown), RNase E appeared to be primarily responsible for removal of the terminator. However, the level of band I increased significantly in the rne-1 rnpA49 double mutant (Figure 6B, lanes 2, 4, 7, 9, 12 and 14), suggesting roles for both RNase E and RNase P in initiating the processing of this transcript. As was seen with the secG leuU transcript (Table 2), the level of the full-length transcript that retained the downstream Rho-independent transcription terminator sequences of the metT operon increased approximately5-fold along with a concomitant reduction in the PF of mature tRNAMet and tRNALeu3 in an rne deletion mutant compared to the temperature-sensitive rne-1 mutant (Figure 6B, lanes 2, 5, 7, 10, 12 and 15, data not shown).
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 61 69 61 69 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 155 163 155 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 206 214 206 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 273 277 273 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metU</italic>
###xml 279 283 279 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glnV</italic>
###xml 288 292 288 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glnX</italic>
###xml 331 336 331 336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 373 385 373 385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1 rnpA49</italic>
###xml 401 409 401 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 453 459 453 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 503 507 503 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glnX</italic>
###xml 570 578 570 578 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 732 740 732 740 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 784 788 784 788 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metU</italic>
###xml 790 798 790 798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
The composition of all the processing intermediates shown in Figure 6B was further confirmed using the additional oligonucleotide probes d, e, f, g and h (Figure 6A). For example, oligonucleotides g and h (Figure 6A), which were specific for the intergenic regions between metU, glnV and glnX, hybridized to bands I and III in the rne-1 single mutant but only to band I in rne-1 rnpA49 double mutant (Figure 6B, lanes 17 and 19, data not shown). In the rnpA49 mutant, the only intermediate observed was glnX containing extra nucleotides at its 5' terminus with probe h (Figure 6B, lane 18). Similarly, while probe d hybridized to bands I, II and IV, probe e hybridized to bands I and II only (data not shown). Furthermore, probe f (Figure 6A) did not hybridize to band III containing metU (Figure 6B, data not shown) suggesting that it was missing the 5' upstream sequences.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 45 53 45 53 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 287 311 287 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT leuW glnU glnW metU</italic>
###xml 349 363 349 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT leuW glnU</italic>
###xml 388 397 388 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT leuW</italic>
###xml 420 424 420 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 540 544 540 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metU</italic>
###xml 558 572 558 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metU glnV glnX</italic>
Taken together, we conclude that the band I (Figure 6B) represents the full-length transcript containing all seven tRNAs. Bands II, IV, V and VI are processing intermediates that retain the 5' non-coding region along with one or more tRNA species. Thus band II has the first five tRNAs (metT leuW glnU glnW metU), band IV has the first three tRNAs (metT leuW glnU), band V had two tRNAs (metT leuW) and band VI has only metT tRNA. On the other hand, band III is derived from the 3' end of the transcript by an RNase P cleavage at 5' end of metU and contains metU glnV glnX as well as the intact Rho-independent transcription terminator.
###end p 67
###begin title 68
DISCUSSION
###end title 68
###begin p 69

###xml 2537 2545 2525 2533 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 2593 2602 2581 2590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 2648 2649 2636 2637 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 2669 2673 2657 2661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 2782 2786 2770 2774 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glnV</italic>
###xml 2791 2795 2779 2783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glnX</italic>
###xml 2968 2972 2956 2960 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu3</sup>
###xml 2978 2981 2966 2969 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 2990 2993 2978 2981 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gln</sup>
###xml 1577 2994 1565 2982 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="70">Processing pathways for the <italic>secG leuU</italic> and <italic>metT</italic> polycistronic transcripts in <italic>E. coli</italic>. (<bold>A</bold>) Processing of the <italic>secG leuU</italic> transcript. The Rho-independent transcription terminator is removed, primarily by RNase E, but can also be cleaved by RNase G. Subsequently, RNase P separates the <italic>leuU</italic> sequence from <italic>secG</italic> generating the mature 5&#8242; end of tRNA<sup>Leu2</sup> and leaving 14 nt downstream of the translation stop codon of <italic>secG</italic>. Final maturation of the 3&#8242; terminus of <italic>leuU</italic> is carried out by a combination of RNase T, RNase PH and RNase D (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>) to generate a mature tRNA<sup>Leu2</sup>. The <italic>secG</italic> mRNA is rapidly degraded exonucleolytically in a process that is dependent primarily on polynucleotide phosphorylase (PNPase) and poly(A) polymerase (PAP I). However, we cannot rule out a role for either RNase II or RNase R at this time. In the absence of RNase P, RNase E can inefficiently cleave at multiple locations with the 14 nt spacer region between <italic>secG</italic> and <italic>leuU</italic>. However, as noted in <xref ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>, only a very small fraction of the full-length <italic>secG leuU</italic> transcript is susceptible to this reaction. (<bold>B</bold>) Processing of the <italic>metT</italic> polycistronic transcript. RNase cleavages remove the Rho-independent transcription terminator and separates <italic>glnV</italic> and <italic>glnX</italic> from the rest of the transcript. RNase P is required to separate the five upstream tRNAs. Subsequent 3&#8242; end processing by RNase T, RNase PH and RNase D generate mature tRNA<sup>Leu3</sup>, tRNA<sup>Met</sup> and tRNA<sup>Gln</sup>.</p>

###xml 2994 2994 2982 2982 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkm991f7"/>
###xml 1568 2994 1556 2982 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F7" position="float"><label>Figure 7.</label><caption><p textid="70">Processing pathways for the <italic>secG leuU</italic> and <italic>metT</italic> polycistronic transcripts in <italic>E. coli</italic>. (<bold>B</bold>) Processing of the <italic>metT</italic> polycistronic transcript. ###xml 74 81 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 938 945 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1653 1660 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Previous studies have identified two distinct tRNA processing pathways in E. coli involving either RNase E or RNase P as the primary endoribonuclease responsible for generating pre-tRNAs from polycistronic transcripts (5,10). In the RNase E-dependent pathway, polycistronic tRNA transcripts are separated into pre-tRNAs solely by RNase E with the pre-tRNAs being subsequently matured at their 5' termini by RNase P (5). In contrast, in the RNase P-dependent pathway, polycistronic tRNA transcripts are separated into pre-tRNAs by RNase P, generating the mature 5' ends in a single step independent of RNase E (10). In this report, we describe for the first time an alternative tRNA processing pathway for the secG leuU and metT (metT leuW glnU glnW metU glnV glnX) polycistronic transcripts (Figure 7A and B) that involves certain aspects of both the RNase E- and RNase P-dependent pathways. What makes this pathway distinct in wild-type E. coli is that the removal of the Rho-independent transcription terminator associated with each polycistronic transcript, primarily by RNase E, significantly stimulates their rapid processing by RNase P into pre-tRNAs containing mature 5' termini. However, RNase E is not absolutely required for this step, in part because RNase G can also remove the terminator sequences and RNase P can inefficiently process a full-length transcript that retains the terminator. The role of RNase G in the removal of the terminator is partially masked by the fact that there is approximately10 times more RNase E in the cell than RNase G (34). Figure 7.Processing pathways for the secG leuU and metT polycistronic transcripts in E. coli. (A) Processing of the secG leuU transcript. The Rho-independent transcription terminator is removed, primarily by RNase E, but can also be cleaved by RNase G. Subsequently, RNase P separates the leuU sequence from secG generating the mature 5' end of tRNALeu2 and leaving 14 nt downstream of the translation stop codon of secG. Final maturation of the 3' terminus of leuU is carried out by a combination of RNase T, RNase PH and RNase D (38) to generate a mature tRNALeu2. The secG mRNA is rapidly degraded exonucleolytically in a process that is dependent primarily on polynucleotide phosphorylase (PNPase) and poly(A) polymerase (PAP I). However, we cannot rule out a role for either RNase II or RNase R at this time. In the absence of RNase P, RNase E can inefficiently cleave at multiple locations with the 14 nt spacer region between secG and leuU. However, as noted in Figure 1, only a very small fraction of the full-length secG leuU transcript is susceptible to this reaction. (B) Processing of the metT polycistronic transcript. RNase cleavages remove the Rho-independent transcription terminator and separates glnV and glnX from the rest of the transcript. RNase P is required to separate the five upstream tRNAs. Subsequent 3' end processing by RNase T, RNase PH and RNase D generate mature tRNALeu3, tRNAMet and tRNAGln.
###end p 69

###begin p 71
###xml 86 90 86 90 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu2</sup>
###xml 96 100 96 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG</italic>
###xml 102 110 102 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 144 153 144 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 244 250 244 250 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 287 292 287 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 294 302 294 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 308 320 308 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne&#916;1018</italic>
###xml 391 395 387 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG</italic>
###xml 433 442 429 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 519 523 515 519 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu2</sup>
###xml 533 541 529 537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 640 644 636 640 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu2</sup>
###xml 680 684 676 680 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG</italic>
Evidence for RNase P being the primary ribonuclease involved in the separation of tRNALeu2 from secG (Figure 7A) was derived from the fact that secG leuU transcripts lacking the Rho-independent transcription terminator (GU2) accumulated in the rnpA49 single mutant but not in either the rne-1 (Figure 1B) or rneDelta1018 deletion strains (data not shown). Furthermore, the identification of secG mRNA fragments with the intact 14 nt secG leuU intergenic sequence along with no unprocessed 5' nucleotides in the pre-tRNALeu2 species (Figure 5, data not shown) confirmed that a single-RNase P cleavage generated the mature 5' terminus of tRNALeu2 and separated it from the upstream secG mRNA.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 110 114 110 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 178 202 178 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT leuV glnU glnW metU</italic>
###xml 220 234 220 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT leuW glnU</italic>
###xml 258 266 258 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 359 367 359 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu2</sup>
###xml 437 441 437 441 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu3</sup>
###xml 450 453 450 453 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 465 471 465 471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 481 490 481 490 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figures 1</xref>
###xml 496 497 496 497 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6</xref>
###xml 548 556 548 556 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
Similarly, inactivation of RNase P led to the dramatic accumulation of several large precursor species of the metT operon (bands II and IV) that contained either the first five (metT leuV glnU glnW metU) or first three (metT leuW glnU) tRNAs, respectively, (Figure 6), suggesting that these tRNAs were also endonucleolytically processed primarily by RNase P (Figure 7B). The significant drop in the RQ and PF of the mature tRNALeu2, tRNALeu3 and tRNAMet species in rnpA49 mutants (Figures 1B and 6B, data not shown) was consistent with this model (Figure 7).
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 441 450 441 450 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figures 1</xref>
###xml 455 456 455 456 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6</xref>
###xml 458 465 458 465 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 535 544 535 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 549 553 549 553 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 895 899 895 899 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glyW</italic>
###xml 904 908 904 908 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">argX</italic>
###xml 936 937 936 937 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 938 939 938 939 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
Interestingly, the presence of a Rho-independent transcription terminator appears to significantly inhibit the ability of RNase P to process both transcripts. This was evidenced by the accumulation of full-length transcripts with intact terminators only in RNase E-deficient strains as opposed to either no accumulation in the wild-type strain or only accumulation of transcripts with the terminator removed in the RNase P-deficient strain (Figures 1 and 6, Table 2). Thus, the role of RNase E and/or RNase G for the processing of the secG leuU and metT polycistronic transcripts is primarily to remove the Rho-independent transcription terminator, thereby facilitating the RNase P-dependent cleavages that generate pre-tRNAs with mature 5' termini. This is in marked contrast to the requirement for initial RNase E cleavages to generate pre-tRNAs with immature 5' ends in the processing of the glyW and argX polycistronic transcripts (5,7).
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 168 175 168 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 403 407 403 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 491 505 491 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metU glnV glnX</italic>
###xml 514 519 514 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 528 536 528 536 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 619 623 619 623 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metU</italic>
###xml 625 633 625 633 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 691 697 691 697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 716 728 716 728 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49 rne-1</italic>
Although it is not clear at this time why the presence of the Rho-independent transcription terminator inhibits RNase P activity, it appears from the data presented in Table 2 that under normal physiological conditions, the terminator sequences are endonucleolytically removed by RNase E and/or RNase G prior to RNase P action to generate the pre-tRNAs. In addition, the last three tRNAs in the complex metT operon are also separated by RNase E as suggested by the accumulation of band III (metU glnV glnX) in the rne-1 strain (Figure 6B). This species was generated by an RNase P cleavage at the mature 5' terminus of metU (Figure 7B, data not shown). The disappearance of this band in the rnpA49 single mutant and rnpA49 rne-1 double mutants supports this interpretation.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 140 149 140 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 162 170 162 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 172 179 172 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 263 270 263 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 387 391 387 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 263 270 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
An unexpected observation was the involvement of RNase G in the removal of the Rho-independent transcription terminator associated with the secG leuU transcript (Figure 4, Table 2). This is the first demonstration that RNase G plays any role in the processing of E. coli transcripts containing tRNAs. While the removal of the Rho-independent transcription terminator associated with the metT polycistronic transcript appeared independent of RNase G activity (data not shown), it seems likely that other polycistronic tRNA transcripts terminated in a Rho-independent fashion may also be partially processed by RNase G.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 194 199 194 199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 415 424 415 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 437 445 437 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 473 482 473 482 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 487 491 487 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 524 533 524 533 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figures 1</xref>
###xml 538 539 538 539 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6</xref>
###xml 548 560 548 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1 rnpA49</italic>
Even though the presence of the Rho-independent transcription terminator inhibited processing by RNase P, the relatively low steady-state level of full-length transcripts of both operons in the rne-1 strain indicates that RNase P can process the full-length transcript, although more slowly than in the presence of functional RNase E. This was consistent with a significant increase in the half-life of full-length secG leuU transcript (Figure 3) and the level of both the secG leuU and metT operon full-length transcripts (Figures 1 and 6) in the rne-1 rnpA49 double mutant compared to either of the single mutants. These results indicate that either RNase E or RNase P can independently initiate the processing of these transcripts, although removal of the Rho-independent transcription terminator is normally the preferred first step in a wild-type strain.
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 347 359 347 355 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne&#916;1018</italic>
###xml 383 388 379 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 441 450 431 440 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 455 459 445 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 526 530 516 520 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu2</sup>
###xml 536 540 526 530 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Leu3</sup>
###xml 549 552 539 542 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 554 562 544 552 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 565 572 555 562 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 653 657 643 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">argX</italic>
###xml 659 678 649 668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">argX hisR leuT proM</italic>
###xml 684 687 674 677 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glW</italic>
###xml 689 703 679 693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glyW cysT leuZ</italic>
###xml 732 737 722 727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1</italic>
###xml 742 754 732 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne&#916;1018</italic>
Our data also clearly show that the temperature-sensitive Rne-1 protein, which is the most widely used allele to characterize which substrates are degraded in an RNase E-dependent fashion, clearly retains significant activity on tRNA substrates at the non-permissive temperature. Thus, there was a 5-6-fold increase in the transcript level in the rneDelta1018 strain compared to the rne-1 strain (2 h after shift to 44degreesC) for both the secG leuU and metT operons as well as concomitant reductions in the PF levels of tRNALeu2, tRNALeu3 and tRNAMet (Figure 6B, Table 2). An independent study from this laboratory has shown identical results for the argX (argX hisR leuT proM) and glW (glyW cysT leuZ) operons when comparing the rne-1 and rneDelta1018 strains (D. Chung, Z. Min, B.-C. Wang and S. R. Kushner, manuscript in preparation).
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 36 43 36 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 64 70 64 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 201 203 201 203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 251 255 251 255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG</italic>
###xml 293 302 293 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 315 324 315 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figures 1</xref>
###xml 329 330 329 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3</xref>
###xml 435 439 435 439 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG</italic>
###xml 548 552 548 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG</italic>
###xml 36 43 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Previous microarray analysis of the E. coli transcriptome in an rnpA49 mutant led to the hypothesis that inactivation of RNase P specifically destabilized transcripts downstream of its cleavage sites (31). However, the dramatic destabilization of the secG mRNA after RNase P processing of the secG leuU transcript (Figures 1 and 3) clearly demonstrates that this idea is not entirely correct. In addition, the failure to stabilize the secG mRNA in any of the endonuclease mutants tested suggests that once the RNase P cleavage occurs, the upstream secG mRNA is rapidly degraded exonucleolytically.
###end p 78
###begin p 79
###xml 153 157 153 157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">leuU</italic>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">leuU</italic>
###xml 227 236 227 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">secG leuU</italic>
###xml 249 258 249 258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figures 1</xref>
###xml 272 273 272 273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7</xref>
###xml 311 319 311 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 411 420 411 420 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figures 5</xref>
###xml 426 427 426 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7</xref>
###xml 445 449 445 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT</italic>
###xml 517 523 517 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnpA49</italic>
###xml 582 594 582 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rne-1 rnpA49</italic>
###xml 610 618 610 618 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 834 838 834 838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glnU</italic>
###xml 843 847 843 847 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glnW</italic>
###xml 919 938 919 938 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metT leuW glnU glnW</italic>
###xml 1019 1023 1019 1023 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glnW</italic>
###xml 1028 1032 1028 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metU</italic>
###xml 1144 1153 1144 1153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">valV valW</italic>
###xml 1158 1172 1158 1172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">leuQ leuP leuV</italic>
###xml 1182 1184 1182 1184 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
Interestingly, a very low level of RNase E cleavages within the intergenic regions of both operons was observed in the absence of RNase P. Thus, the pre-leuU species were the result of RNase E cleavages upstream of leuU in the secG leuU transcript (Figures 1B, lane 3 and 7A). These cleavages were inefficient (Figure 1B, lane 3), occurred at multiple sites, and probably did not take place in wild-type cells (Figures 5C and 7A). Similarly for metT operon, the presence of precursors (bands II, IV, V and VI) in the rnpA49 single mutant and the reduction in their intensity in the rne-1 rnpA49 double mutant (Figure 6B) suggest that RNase E can also cleave in the intercistronic regions among the first five tRNAs with varying efficiencies. For example, the presence of a large amount of band IV indicates efficient cleavage between glnU and glnW, while the absence of an intermediate containing the first four tRNAs (metT leuW glnU glnW) suggests that RNase E is unable to cleave in the intercistronic region between glnW and metU. Similar inefficient cleavages of RNase P-dependent tRNA transcripts by RNase E have also been observed in the valV valW and leuQ leuP leuV operons (10).
###end p 79

sites that have been mapped.</p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
With the work presented here, RNase E cleavage sites and relative efficiencies of cleavage are now available for 19/86 tRNA species (Table 3). This data is of particular interest because previous work has suggested the importance of an A/U-rich region in the cleavage site (35,36) and the presence of a G residue at the -2 position and either C or U at the +2 position (37). Of the 12 high-efficiency RNase E cleavage sites only one has a G at the -2 position. In contrast, 9/12 sites have a C or U at the +2 position (Table 3). In addition, it does not appear that RNase E can cleave closer than 1 nt downstream of the CCA determinant, even if the next nucleotide is a U. ###end p 80
###begin p 81
Analysis of RNase E cleavage sites in tRNA precursors
###end p 81
###begin p 82
Downward arrows indicate RNase E cleavage sites that have been mapped.
###end p 82
###begin p 83
###xml 77 86 77 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">valV valW</italic>
###xml 91 105 91 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">leuQ leuP leuV</italic>
###xml 115 117 115 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 338 342 338 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metZ</italic>
###xml 351 365 351 365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">metZ metW metV</italic>
###xml 479 484 479 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 487 489 487 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 736 738 736 738 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 924 931 924 931 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 924 931 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Based on the experiments reported above and our recent observations with the valV valW and leuQ leuP leuV operons (10), it is now clear that a significant number of tRNA precursors are dependent on RNase P for their initial separation from polycistronic transcripts rather than RNase E. In fact, a preliminary analysis indicates that the metZ operon (metZ metW metV) is also highly dependent on RNase P for processing (data not shown) as predicted from the microarray data of Li et al. (33). These observations provide further support for our hypothesis that the essential function of RNase P may be related to its requirement for the processing of polycistronic tRNA transcripts rather than the processing of the 5' ends of pre-tRNAs (10). Finally, it would not be surprising if there were, in fact still yet, unidentified additional pathways for the maturation of specific tRNAs. Thus the mechanisms of tRNA maturation in E. coli are far more diverse than has previously been envisioned.
###end p 83
